Although there may be enough variation\n\nin the cavity gas speed of sound to provide the necessary variation in tune\nfrequency.\n\n5.\n\nAcoustic Liner Problem Areas\nAcoustic damper problems fall into two general categories:\n\n(1)\nthose problems associated with the determining of the gaseous environment\n\nimposed on the resonator by combustion, and (2) those problems due to geometry\nand physical limitations of the system. The first category makes designing\nHelmholtz resonators difficult due to presence of unknowns, due to transient\nvariations, and due to uncontrollable and/or hostile conditions.\n\nThe second\n\ncategory causes problems in the design of a liner due generally to limitations\nin the number, size, location, tune, and absorption coefficient frequency\nbandwidth of the resonators.\na.\n\nGaseous Environment\nThe gaseous environmental parameters affecting acoustic liner\n\ndesign consist primarily of the following:\n\n( ) cavity gas temperatures, (2)\n1\n\ncavity gas composition, (3) mean gas flow past the liner aperture, ( 4 ) mean\ngas flow through the liner aperture, and (5) the sound pressure level of the\nresonant combustion.\nThe first two parameters, cavity gas temperature and composition (MR), are not always measured or are measured only indirectly and not\nnecessarily as a function of time. Generally, the first two parameters are\ntransients and can vary by a factor of two, even during steady state operation.\nThis result implies that the speed of sound used to tune the resonator design\n\nPage 132\n\nReport 8852-FR\n\nV, F, A c o u s t i c s ( c o n t . )\nw i l l v a r y by a f a c t o r e q u a l t o t h e s q u a r e r o o t of two, o r about - 40%. However,\n+\nt h e e r r o r i s n o t g e n e r a l l y t h a t g r e a t due t o t h e compromise between t e m p e r a t u r e\nand MR, g e n e r a l l y found a s shown i n F i g u r e 4 9 .\n\nNote t h a t f o r a t y p i c a l r o c k e t\n\nl i n e r t h e speed of sound i s almost c o n s t a n t as t h e m i x t u r e r a t i o and temperat u r e change.\n\nUnless some means o f s t a b i l i z i n g t h e c a v i t y g a s t e m p e r a t u r e\nand composition o r speed of sound i s u s e d , some o t h e r allowance must b e made\nf o r "off tuned" r e s o n a t o r s .\n\nM u l t i p l e r e s o n a t o r frequency t u n e s and g e o m e t r i e s\n\nand v e r y l a r g e amounts of r e s o n a t o r s c a n s u f f i c e a l s o .\n\nThe l a s t t h r e e p a r a m e t e r s a l l have t h e e f f e c t of i n c r e a s i n g\nt h e r e s o n a n t f r e q u e n c y of t h e r e s o n a t o r and d e c r e a s i n g t h e r e s o n a n t a b s o r p t i o n\nw i t h i n c r e a s i n g g a s v e l o c i t y o r sound p r e s s u r e l e v e l .\n\nThe resonance frequency\n\ncan b e i n c r e a s e d as much as 63% above t h e nonflow c o n d i t i o n f o r t h i n a p e r t u r e s\nw i t h about 300 f t l s e c g a s v e l o c i t y p a s t t h e a p e r t u r e , o r about 15 f t / s e c gas\nv e l o c i t y t h r o u g h t h e a p e r t u r e , o r about 15 f t / s e c o s c i l l a t o r y (S.P.L.)\nv e l o c i t y i n the a p e r t u r e .\n\ngas\n\nSuch r e s o n a n t frequency changes are n e a r l y i m p o s s i b l e\n\nt o measure i n a h o t f i r i n g r o c k e t engine.\n\nThe amount of frequency s h i f t i s\n\na l s o a f u n c t i o n of t h e a p e r t u r e L/D ( s e e Appendix I, Design Guide) and\ncontour.\n\nI f t h e maximum r e s o n a n t frequency s h i f t i s assumed, t h e n t h e\n\naccompanying increase i n t h e a p e r t u r e \' s a c o u s t i c r e s i s t a n c e becomes s o g r e a t\nt h a t the r e s o n The optimum resonator cavity backing distance (or volume) is the maximum that can be tuned.\n\nSince tuning requires,\n\nfor a constant open area, that the product of the aperture thickness and the\ncavity backing distance be a constant, then minimizing the aperture thickness\nrequires a maximizing of the cavity backing distance. Backing distance is\ngenerally not a problem due to the fact that the aperture thickness is usually\nso thick that the backing distance is of the same order of size.\n\n6.\n\nAcoustic Liner Design Criteria\nHelmholtz resonator design criteria have three major objectives:\n\n( ) t o optimize the acoustic damping, (2) to be compatible with the other\n1\nsystem requirements, and ( 3 ) to be economically feasible to fabricate. The\nfirst objective is approximated by considering all the analytical methods of\noptimizing the design parameters, and comparing each with previous experimental\nresults. The second objective is equally intangible but is usually conservatively selected to insure reliability of the liner design with respect to heat\ntransfer and structural considerations.
